**Input Analysis**
- Field: Age
- Type: Numeric (integer)
- Range: 18 to 60
- Step: 1 (integer precision)

**BVA Test Cases**

| Test Case ID | Input Value | Expected Result | Boundary Type |
|---|---|---|---|
| TC-01 | 17 | Invalid | Just below minimum |
| TC-02 | 18 | Valid | Minimum boundary |
| TC-03 | 19 | Valid | Just above minimum |
| TC-04 | 59 | Valid | Just below maximum |
| TC-05 | 60 | Valid | Maximum boundary |
| TC-06 | 61 | Invalid | Just above maximum |

---

**Why these values matter:**

- **TC-01 (17)** — Verifies the system rejects users who are underage by 1 year. This is your most critical rejection test near the lower bound.
- **TC-02 (18)** — Confirms the minimum valid age is accepted. A common bug is using `>` instead of `>=`, which would incorrectly reject 18.
- **TC-03 (19)** — Sanity check that values just inside the lower boundary work correctly.
- **TC-04 (59)** — Sanity check that values just inside the upper boundary work correctly.
- **TC-05 (60)** — Confirms the maximum valid age is accepted. Same off-by-one risk as TC-02 but on the upper end.
- **TC-06 (61)** — Verifies the system rejects ages above the limit by 1 year.

---

> 💡 **Tip:** You may also want to add edge-case tests for non-numeric inputs (e.g., `"abc"`, empty string, `null`) and extreme values (e.g., `0`, `-1`, `999`) to cover input validation beyond BVA boundaries.
---

1. The output includes boundary values 17, 18, 19, 59, 60, 61

3. The output is presented in a structured table format

Respond in this exact JSON format (no markdown, no code fences):
{
  "assertion_results": [

|-----------|-------|----------|-----------|
| Valid middle value | `35` | Valid | Inside range |
| Below minimum | `10` | Invalid | Below range |
| Above maximum | `75` | Invalid | Above range |

### Edge / Invalid Input Cases
| Test Case | Input | Expected | Reason |
|-----------|-------|----------|--------|
| Zero | `0` | Invalid | Out of range |
| Negative | `-1` | Invalid | Out of range |

| Decimal | `25.5` | Invalid or truncated | Type validation |
| Non-numeric | `abc` | Invalid | Type validation |
| Very large number | `999` | Invalid | Out of range |
| Leading zeros | `018` | Invalid or `18` | Parsing behavior |
| Whitespace only | `   ` | Invalid | Required field |

### Summary of partitions
- **Valid**: 18–60 (inclusive)
- **Invalid — too young**: < 18
- **Invalid — too old**: > 60
- **Invalid — bad type**: non-integer, empty, non-numeric

The most critical cases are the **boundary values** (17, 18, 60, 61) — these catch off-by-one errors which are the most common bugs in range validation.

|---|---|---|---|
| TC-01 | 08:59 | ❌ Invalid | Just below minimum |
| TC-02 | 09:00 | ✅ Valid | Minimum boundary |
| TC-03 | 09:01 | ✅ Valid | Just above minimum |

---

## Why These Values Matter

| Boundary | Risk Being Tested |
|---|---|
| **08:59** | Ensures the system rejects bookings before opening hours |
| **09:00** | Confirms the first valid booking slot is accepted (off-by-one risk) |
| **09:01** | Verifies normal early-morning bookings work after the boundary |
| **16:59** | Confirms the last valid slot before closing is accepted |
| **17:00** | Validates whether closing time itself is bookable (confirm intent with your team!) |
| **17:01** | Ensures the system blocks bookings after closing hours |

## USER (2026-03-27 20:08:04)

I have an input field for "comments". Help me create BVA test cases.

## ASSISTANT (2026-03-27 20:08:15)

[no response]

## USER (2026-03-27 20:08:19)

Grade each assertion against the actual output below.
For each assertion, respond with PASS or FAIL and brief evidence.

ACTUAL OUTPUT:
---
## Input Analysis — Comments Field

The **Comments** field is a **free text input**, which means it doesn't have numeric or time-based boundaries. BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is designed specifically for fields with numeric or time ranges (e.g., age 18–60, price 0.00–999.99, time 00:00–23:59).

Applying BVA here wouldn't be meaningful — there's no "just below minimum" or "just above maximum" for open-ended text.

---

## Recommended Alternatives

Here are techniques better suited for a Comments field:

| Technique | Best For |
|---|---|
| **Equivalence Partitioning** | Grouping valid/invalid input categories (e.g., empty, normal text, special characters) |
| **Boundary Value Analysis** | *Only* if there's a **character limit** (e.g., max 500 characters) |
| **Exploratory Testing** | Uncovering unexpected behavior with edge-case inputs |
| **Error Guessing** | Testing known risky inputs like SQL injection, XSS scripts, emojis, newlines |

---

## How I Can Help — Just Answer One Question

Does your **Comments** field have a **character limit**?

- ✅ **Yes, e.g. max 500 characters** → I can apply BVA on the character count (e.g., 0, 1, 499, 500, 501 characters)
- ❌ **No limit / unknown** → I'll generate Equivalence Partitioning test cases instead (empty, short, long, special chars, etc.)
---

ASSERTIONS:
1. The output recognizes that a free-text field is not suitable for BVA
2. The output asks for clarification or suggests alternative testing techniques

Respond in this exact JSON format (no markdown, no code fences):
{
  "assertion_results": [
    {"text": "assertion text", "passed": true/false, "evidence": "brief quote or reason"}
  ]
}

| 2 | At minimum | 0% | Accepted | Valid (lower bound) |

| 5 | Just below maximum | 49% | Accepted | Valid (upper bound - 1) |
| 6 | At maximum | 50% | Accepted | Valid (upper bound) |
| 7 | Just above maximum | 51% | Rejected / error | Invalid (upper bound + 1) |
| 8 | Far above maximum | 100% | Rejected / error | Invalid (far above) |

### Key boundaries

- **Lower boundary:** 0% — test at `-1`, `0`, `1`
- **Upper boundary:** 50% — test at `49`, `50`, `51`

### Notes

- If fractional inputs are allowed (e.g. 50.1%), add test cases at `49.9%`, `50.0%`, and `50.1%`
- If the field is an integer-only input, `51` is sufficient for the over-limit case

## Age Field Test Cases (Valid range: 18–60)

| ID | Input | Expected | Technique |

---
Here are test cases for a booking system time input (09:00–17:00):

## Boundary Values

| Input | Expected | Rationale |
|-------|----------|-----------|
| `09:00` | Accept | Lower bound |
| `17:00` | Accept | Upper bound |
| `08:59` | Reject | One minute before open |
| `17:01` | Reject | One minute after close |

## Valid Inputs (within range)

| Input | Expected |
|-------|----------|
| `09:01` | Accept |
| `12:00` | Accept |
| `16:59` | Accept |

## Invalid Format

| Input | Expected | Rationale |
|-------|----------|-----------|
| `9:00` | Reject | Missing leading zero |
| `09:0` | Reject | Single digit minute |
| `9` | Reject | Time only, no minutes |
| `0900` | Reject | No colon separator |
| `09-00` | Reject | Wrong separator |
| `09:60` | Reject | Minute out of range |
| `25:00` | Reject | Hour out of range |
| `abc` | Reject | Non-numeric |
| `` | Reject | Empty input |
| `null` / `undefined` | Reject | Missing input |

## Ambiguous / Edge Cases

| Input | Expected | Rationale |
|-------|----------|-----------|
| `09:00:00` | Clarify | Seconds included — accept or reject? |
| `09:00 AM` | Clarify | 12-hour format — does the system support it? |
| `17:00:01` | Reject | One second over |
| `00:00` | Reject | Midnight, outside range |
| `13:00` | Accept | 1 PM in 24h format |

## Questions to Clarify with the Team

1. **Are seconds allowed?** (`09:00:00`)
2. **Is `17:00` bookable or is it the cutoff?** (i.e., can someone book the last slot *at* 17:00?)
3. **What's the slot duration?** A 30-min slot starting at 16:45 ends at 17:15 — is that valid?
4. **12-hour format support?** (`9:00 AM` vs `09:00`)
5. **Timezone handling?** If applicable, whose timezone is validated?

The boundary and invalid-format cases are the highest priority — the ambiguous ones need product decisions before you can write assertions.

## USER (2026-03-28 00:43:39)

I have an input field for "comments". Help me create BVA test cases.

## ASSISTANT (2026-03-28 00:43:48)

[no response]

## USER (2026-03-28 00:43:53)

Grade each assertion against the actual output below.
For each assertion, respond with PASS or FAIL and brief evidence.

ACTUAL OUTPUT:
---
## Input Analysis

- **Field**: Comments
- **Type**: Free text

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is **not the appropriate technique** for a free-text field like "Comments." BVA is designed for fields with **numeric or time-based ranges** (e.g., age, price, duration), where you can define a minimum and maximum value with discrete steps.

---

## Suggested Alternatives

Here are better techniques for testing a free-text "Comments" field:

| Technique | Best For | Example |
|---|---|---|
| **Equivalence Partitioning** | Grouping valid/invalid input classes | Empty string, normal text, special characters |
| **Boundary Value Analysis (length)** | If there's a **character limit** (e.g., max 500 chars) | 0, 1, 499, 500, 501 characters |
| **Exploratory Testing** | Uncovering unexpected behavior | SQL injection, emoji, Unicode, line breaks |
| **Decision Table Testing** | Field behavior depends on conditions | Required vs. optional based on another field |

---

## How I Can Help

If your "Comments" field has a **character length constraint**, BVA *can* apply! For example:

> *"Comments must be between 10 and 500 characters"*

👉 **Do you have a minimum or maximum character length for this field?** If so, share it and I'll generate a full BVA test case table for you!
---

ASSERTIONS:
1. The output recognizes that a free-text field is not suitable for BVA
2. The output asks for clarification or suggests alternative testing techniques

Respond in this exact JSON format (no markdown, no code fences):
{
  "assertion_results": [
    {"text": "assertion text", "passed": true/false, "evidence": "brief quote or reason"}
  ]
}

| TC-01 | Before opening time | Enter 08:59, which is one minute before the earliest allowed appointment time of 09:00. The system should reject this input. | 08:59 | Invalid - rejected |
| TC-02 | Opening time boundary | Enter 09:00, which is the earliest allowed appointment time. The system should accept this input. | 09:00 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-03 | Just after opening time | Enter 09:01, which is one minute after the opening boundary. The system should accept this input. | 09:01 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-04 | Just before closing time | Enter 16:59, which is one minute before the latest allowed appointment time of 17:00. The system should accept this input. | 16:59 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-05 | Closing time boundary | Enter 17:00, which is the latest allowed appointment time. The system should accept this input. | 17:00 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-06 | After closing time | Enter 17:01, which is one minute past the latest allowed appointment time of 17:00. The system should reject this input. | 17:01 | Invalid - rejected |

---

**6 test cases** cover all four critical boundary points. A few additional scenarios worth considering for your booking system:

- **Midnight boundary** (00:00) — to ensure times from a different day are rejected
- **Invalid time formats** (e.g., `9:00`, `25:00`, `abc`) — if the field accepts free text input
- **Empty/null input** — if the field is optional

   - **Exploratory Testing** — test edge cases like emojis, HTML/script injection, line breaks, copy-pasted content.

## Input Analysis

- **Field**: Comments
- **Type**: Free text (string)

BVA is **not the right technique** for a free-text "comments" field. Boundary Value Analysis applies to fields with **numeric or time-based ranges** (e.g., age, price, booking time) — it relies on a measurable min/max with a defined step size.

---

## Better Techniques for a Text Field

Here are more suitable approaches depending on what you want to test:

| Technique | Best for | Example test ideas |
|---|---|---|
| **Equivalence Partitioning** | Grouping valid/invalid inputs | Empty string, normal text, only spaces |
| **BVA on length** | If there's a character limit | 0 chars, 1 char, max-1, max, max+1 |
| **Exploratory Testing** | Edge cases in content | Special characters, emojis, SQL injection, very long strings, HTML tags |
| **Boundary on length** | Max/min character constraints | Requires knowing the min/max character limit |

---

## What I Can Help With

If your "comments" field has a **character length constraint** (e.g., minimum 10 characters, maximum 500 characters), I *can* apply BVA on the **length** of the input.

**Could you tell me:**
> Does your comments field have a minimum or maximum character limit? (e.g., "must be between 10 and 500 characters")

If yes, I'll generate full BVA test cases based on those length boundaries. If there's no length constraint, I'd recommend **Equivalence Partitioning** or **Exploratory Testing** instead — and I can help with those too! 😊

## Input Analysis

- **Field**: Comments
- **Type**: Free text

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is designed for fields with **numeric or time-based boundaries** — it works by testing values just below, at, and just above a minimum or maximum number.

A **"comments" free-text field** doesn't have numeric or time boundaries by nature, so BVA is not the appropriate technique here.

---

### What I'd suggest instead:

| Scenario | Better Technique |
|---|---|
| No character limit constraints | **Equivalence Partitioning** (e.g., empty, typical text, special characters, whitespace-only) |
| Has a character limit (e.g., max 500 chars) | **BVA can apply!** — treating character count as the numeric boundary |
| Testing content types/formats | **Exploratory Testing** (e.g., emojis, HTML injection, line breaks) |

---

### Can we apply BVA?

If your comments field **does have a character limit**, I can absolutely generate BVA test cases for it! Just let me know:

1. **Is there a minimum character count?** (e.g., must be at least 1 character, or can it be empty?)
2. **Is there a maximum character count?** (e.g., max 500 characters)

With those two numbers, I'll generate the full BVA test case table for you. 😊

ASSERTIONS:

| 3 | Above minimum by 1 | `15,001` | Accepted | Min + 1 |
| 4 | Nominal (midpoint) | `107,500` | Accepted | Nominal |
| 5 | Below maximum by 1 | `199,999` | Accepted | Max - 1 |
| 6 | Exact maximum | `200,000` | Accepted | Max |
| 7 | Above maximum by 1 | `200,001` | Rejected | Max + 1 |

### Additional robustness cases

| # | Test Case | Input | Expected Result | Reason |
|---|-----------|-------|-----------------|--------|
| 8 | Zero | `0` | Rejected | Well below min |
| 9 | Negative | `-1` | Rejected | Negative value |
| 10 | Decimal | `15000.50` | Rejected | Not integer |
| 11 | Empty/null | _(blank)_ | Rejected | Required field |
| 12 | Non-numeric | `"abc"` | Rejected | Wrong type |

### Summary

- **Valid inputs (must pass):** 15,000 / 15,001 / 107,500 / 199,999 / 200,000
- **Invalid inputs (must be rejected):** 14,999 / 200,001 / 0 / -1 / 15000.50 / blank / "abc"

Cases 1–7 are the core BVA set. Cases 8–12 cover type/null safety — include them if the field is user-facing or comes from an API.

## Boundary Value Analysis

| ID | Input | Partition | Expected Result |
|----|-------|-----------|-----------------|
| TC-07 | 35 | Valid (18–60) | Accepted |
| TC-08 | 10 | Invalid below (<18) | Rejected |
| TC-09 | 75 | Invalid above (>60) | Rejected |

| ID | Input | Type | Expected Result |
|----|-------|------|-----------------|
| TC-10 | 0 | Zero | Rejected |
| TC-11 | -1 | Negative | Rejected |

## Notes

- **TC-14 (decimal)**: Decide whether to truncate, round, or reject. Most registration forms reject non-integer ages.
- **TC-15 (leading zero)**: Some parsers treat `018` as octal (= 16), which would fail validation unexpectedly — worth a negative test.
- **Priority order**: TC-02, TC-05 (exact boundaries) and TC-01, TC-06 (just outside) are the most critical — they catch off-by-one errors in the validation logic.

## Input Analysis

- **Type**: Free text (string)
- **BVA applicable**: ❌ Not directly applicable

BVA is designed for **numeric or time-based inputs** where boundaries like min/max values can be tested with a "1 step" increment. A free-text "comments" field doesn't have numeric boundaries by nature, so BVA isn't the right technique here.

---

### Two paths forward:

**Option A — You have a character length limit** (e.g., "comments must be between 10 and 500 characters")

If your system enforces a **minimum and/or maximum character count**, BVA *is* applicable! The boundaries would be on the **number of characters**.

👉 Please tell me the **min and/or max character length** for the comments field, and I'll generate the full BVA test cases for you.

---

**Option B — No length constraint / pure free text**

If there's no character limit, consider these more suitable techniques instead:

| Technique | Best for |
|---|---|
| **Equivalence Partitioning** | Valid vs. invalid input classes (e.g., empty, normal text, special characters) |
| **Exploratory Testing** | Edge cases like emojis, SQL injection, XSS, very long strings, Unicode |
| **Decision Table Testing** | When comments interact with other fields or trigger conditional logic |

---

Which option fits your situation? Or feel free to share more details about how the comments field behaves in your system!
---

1. The output recognizes that a free-text field is not suitable for BVA

| # | Test Case | Input (฿) | Expected Result | Boundary Point |

ACTUAL OUTPUT:
---
## Input Analysis

- **Field**: Comments
- **Type**: Free text

A "comments" field is a **free-text input**, which means BVA is **not the right technique** for its content — BVA requires numeric or time-based boundaries to work with.

### Why BVA Doesn't Apply Here

BVA works by stepping one unit above/below a boundary (e.g., 17/18/19 for an age limit of 18). Free-text has no such numeric boundary on its *content*, so there's nothing to step across.

---

### ✅ Better Alternatives for a Comments Field

| Technique | Best for |
|---|---|
| **Equivalence Partitioning** | Grouping valid vs. invalid inputs (e.g., empty, normal text, special characters, HTML/script injection) |
| **Exploratory Testing** | Checking behavior with emoji, Unicode, line breaks, copy-pasted content |
| **Boundary Value Analysis** *(applicable if there's a character limit)* | If the field has a min/max character count (e.g., 10–500 characters), BVA applies to the **length** |

---

### 🔍 One Exception — Character Length Limit

If your "comments" field has a **character limit**, BVA *can* apply to the number of characters. For example, if the field accepts 10 to 500 characters, I can generate test cases like:

| Input length | Example | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 9 characters | `"Hello!!!"` | Invalid |
| 10 characters | `"Hello!!!!"`| Valid |
| 500 characters | *(500-char string)* | Valid |
| 501 characters | *(501-char string)* | Invalid |

---

**Does your comments field have a minimum or maximum character limit?**
If yes, share the limits and I'll generate complete BVA test cases right away. If not, I'd recommend using **Equivalence Partitioning** instead — just say the word and I'll help with that too!
---

ASSERTIONS:
1. The output recognizes that a free-text field is not suitable for BVA
2. The output asks for clarification or suggests alternative testing techniques

Respond in this exact JSON format (no markdown, no code fences):
{
  "assertion_results": [
    {"text": "assertion text", "passed": true/false, "evidence": "brief quote or reason"}
  ]
}

Before generating the BVA table, I need to clarify the **precision of the age field**, because it directly determines what the boundary values are.

**Two common interpretations:**

| Interpretation | Input Type | Boundary "just below 65" |

**Why it matters:**

- If the field accepts **age as an integer** (whole years), the boundary values are `64`, `65`, `66`.
- If the field accepts a **birthdate** (e.g. `1960-03-28`), the system derives age dynamically, and the boundary falls at the exact date when a person turns 65 years old — meaning `64y 11m 29d` (today's date minus 65 years + 1 day) is the last valid day.

These produce completely different test cases and different test data.

**Please confirm:**
1. Does the user enter their **age as a number** (integer field)?
2. Or does the user enter their **date of birth** (date field, and age is calculated)?
---

ASSERTIONS:
1. The output asks the user to clarify the minimum unit or precision of age (e.g. whole years vs birthdate with year-month-day)
2. The output explains how different precision levels lead to different boundary values
3. The output does not generate a final BVA table before the user confirms the precision

Respond in this exact JSON format (no markdown, no code fences):
{
  "assertion_results": [
    {"text": "assertion text", "passed": true/false, "evidence": "brief quote or reason"}
  ]
}

## Current SKILL.md
```markdown
---
name: test-engineer
description: >
  Helps business users and technical users analyze requirements with numeric or time inputs,
  then generates test cases and test data using Boundary Value Analysis (BVA) technique.
  Use when the user asks for test cases, test data, BVA, boundary testing, or wants to
  verify input fields with numeric ranges or time ranges.
license: Apache-2.0
metadata:
  author: bomb-skills
  version: "0.1"
---

## Overview

You are a test engineer assistant that uses **Boundary Value Analysis (BVA)** to generate test cases for input fields with numeric or time boundaries. Your goal is to save users time by automatically identifying boundaries and generating structured, ready-to-use test cases.

## When to Activate

Activate when the user:
- Asks for test cases for a field with a numeric or time range
- Mentions boundary value analysis, BVA, or boundary testing
- Provides requirements with min/max constraints on inputs
- Wants to verify input validation for numeric or time fields

## Instructions

### Step 1: Analyze the Requirement

Read the user's requirement and identify:
- **Input type**: numeric (integer or decimal) or time (HH:MM or HH:MM:SS)
- **Minimum value**: the lowest valid value
- **Maximum value**: the highest valid value
- **Precision**: integer, decimal places, or time unit (minutes/seconds)

If the input is not numeric or time-based (e.g., free text, dropdowns), inform the user that BVA is not the appropriate technique and suggest alternatives like Equivalence Partitioning or exploratory testing.

If the minimum value is greater than the maximum value, flag this as a likely error and ask the user to clarify before proceeding.

If there are multiple input fields, analyze each field separately and organize the output by field.

#### Ambiguous Precision / Minimum Unit

If the requirement does **not** make the minimum unit (precision/step size) clear, do NOT assume a default. Instead, ask the user to clarify before generating test cases. The minimum unit determines the "1 step" used in BVA and directly changes the test data.

**When precision IS clear** — go ahead and generate test cases without asking:
- The user specifies the format explicitly (e.g., "integer", "2 decimal places", "HH:MM")
- The user provides boundary values with a visible format (e.g., "09:00 to 17:00" implies HH:MM, "0.01 to 9999.99" implies 2 decimals)
- The context is unambiguous for domains without multiple interpretations (e.g., "quantity 1 to 100" is clearly integer — there's no alternative interpretation)

**When precision IS ambiguous** — always ask the user before proceeding:
- **Age** — always ambiguous, even if given as integers like "18 to 60". Age could mean: (a) user types age as a whole number, or (b) user enters a birthdate and the system calculates age in years-months-days. These produce very different boundary values. Always ask.
- **Money** — ambiguous unless decimal places are explicit. "Limit 30,000 baht" could mean step of 0.01, 1, or 100.
- **Percentage** — ambiguous unless format is stated. Could be integer (step=1) or decimal (step=0.01).
- Any domain where the data type could reasonably be interpreted multiple ways.

When asking:
1. Identify that the precision is ambiguous.
2. Show the user **concrete examples** of how different precision choices produce different boundary values.
3. Ask them to confirm which precision matches their system.
4. Wait for the user's response before generating test cases.

Common ambiguous cases:
- **Age**: Is the input a whole number of years (step = 1 year), or a birthdate where age is calculated in years-months-days? If birthdate, the boundary is not "64 years" but "64 years, 11 months, 29 days" — which means the actual input field is a date, not a number.
- **Money**: Is the minimum unit 0.01 (satang/cents), 1 (whole baht/dollars), or a larger denomination like 100? For a limit of 30,000: step=0.01 gives 29,999.99, step=1 gives 29,999, step=100 gives 29,900.
- **Percentage**: Is it integer (step=1) or decimal (step=0.01, 0.1)?

#### Single-Bound Requirements

If the requirement specifies **only a lower limit** (e.g., "must be at least 0") or **only an upper limit** (e.g., "cannot exceed 50"), do NOT generate the full BVA table immediately. Instead:

1. Tell the user which bound you found (lower or upper) and its value.
2. Ask the user to confirm or provide the missing bound. For example:
   - "I found a lower limit of 0, but no upper limit. What is the maximum allowed value for this field?"
   - "I found an upper limit of 50%, but no lower limit. What is the minimum allowed value? (e.g., 0?)"
3. Wait for the user's response before generating test cases.
4. Once both bounds are confirmed, proceed to Step 2 as normal.

### Step 2: Apply BVA Technique

For each identified boundary (min, max), generate these **6 core boundary values**:

| Position | Value | Expected Result |
|---|---|---|
| Just below minimum | min - 1 step | Invalid |
| Minimum (boundary) | min | Valid |
| Just above minimum | min + 1 step | Valid |
| Just below maximum | max - 1 step | Valid |
| Maximum (boundary) | max | Valid |
| Just above maximum | max + 1 step | Invalid |

Where "1 step" depends on precision:
- **Integer**: step = 1
- **Decimal (N places)**: step = 10^(-N) (e.g., 2 decimal places → 0.01)
- **Time (HH:MM)**: step = 1 minute
- **Time (HH:MM:SS)**: step = 1 second

### Step 3: Generate Output

Present the test cases in a **markdown table** with these 5 columns:

| ID | Name | Description | Input | Expected Output |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| TC-01 | {short name} | {business description} | {value} | {result} |

Column definitions:
- **ID**: Sequential test case ID (TC-01, TC-02, ...)
- **Name**: Short name describing what this test case covers (e.g., "Below minimum age", "Maximum boundary")
- **Description**: Business-understandable explanation of what is being tested and what should happen. Write it so a non-technical person can understand the purpose. Example: "Enter age 17, which is one below the minimum allowed age of 18. The system should reject this input."
- **Input**: The concrete test data value, ready to copy-paste
- **Expected Output**: Whether the system should accept or reject the value (e.g., "Invalid - rejected", "Valid - accepted")

## Example

**User prompt**: "Age field accepts 18 to 60"

**Output**:

**Input Analysis**
- Field: Age
- Type: Numeric (integer)
- Range: 18 to 60

**BVA Test Cases**

| ID | Name | Description | Input | Expected Output |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| TC-01 | Below minimum age | Enter age 17, which is one below the minimum allowed age of 18. The system should reject this input. | 17 | Invalid - rejected |
| TC-02 | Minimum age boundary | Enter age 18, which is the lowest allowed age. The system should accept this input. | 18 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-03 | Above minimum age | Enter age 19, which is just above the minimum. The system should accept this input. | 19 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-04 | Below maximum age | Enter age 59, which is just below the maximum allowed age of 60. The system should accept this input. | 59 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-05 | Maximum age boundary | Enter age 60, which is the highest allowed age. The system should accept this input. | 60 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-06 | Above maximum age | Enter age 61, which is one above the maximum allowed age of 60. The system should reject this input. | 61 | Invalid - rejected |

## Example: Single-Bound Requirement

**User prompt**: "The score field must be at least 0. Generate BVA test cases."

**Output**:

**Input Analysis**
- Field: Score
- Type: Numeric
- Lower limit: 0
- Upper limit: **not specified**

I found a lower limit of **0**, but no upper limit was provided. To generate complete BVA test cases, I need both boundaries.

**Could you confirm the maximum allowed value for the score field?** For example, is it 100, 999, or something else?

## Example: Ambiguous Precision

**User prompt**: "Registration requires users to be not over 65 years old. Create BVA test cases."

**Output**:

**Input Analysis**
- Field: Age
- Constraint: not over 65 years old
- Precision: **unclear — need to clarify**

Before I generate test cases, I need to clarify the **minimum unit of age data** in your system, because it changes the boundary values significantly:

| If the input is... | Step size | Boundary just below 65 | Boundary at 65 | Boundary just above 65 |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Age as whole years (integer) | 1 year | 64 | 65 | 66 |
| Birthdate (year-month-day) | 1 day | 64 years, 11 months, 29 days | Exactly 65 years | 65 years, 0 months, 1 day |

**How does your system capture age?**
- Does the user enter their age as a number (e.g., "64")? → I'll use integer step of 1 year.
- Does the user enter a birthdate and the system calculates age? → I'll use date-based boundaries and the input field is actually a date.

## Example: Ambiguous Money Precision

**User prompt**: "Daily deposit limit is not over 30,000 baht. Generate BVA test cases."

**Output**:

**Input Analysis**
- Field: Deposit amount
- Constraint: not over 30,000 baht
- Precision: **unclear — need to clarify**

Before I generate test cases, I need to clarify the **minimum unit of money** your system accepts:

| If the minimum unit is... | Boundary just below 30,000 | At 30,000 | Just above 30,000 |
|---|---|---|---|
| 0.01 (satang) | 29,999.99 | 30,000.00 | 30,000.01 |
| 1 (whole baht) | 29,999 | 30,000 | 30,001 |
| 100 (hundred baht) | 29,900 | 30,000 | 30,100 |

**What is the smallest amount a user can deposit?** For example, can they deposit 0.01 baht (satang), or only whole baht, or only multiples of 100?

```

```
## Input Analysis

- **Field**: Comments
- **Type**: Free text

A "comments" field is a **free-text input**, which means BVA is **not the right technique** for its content — BVA requires numeric or time-based boundaries to work with.

### Why BVA Doesn't Apply Here

BVA works by stepping one unit above/below a boundary (e.g., 17/18/19 for an age limit of 18). Free-text has no such numeric boundary on its *content*, so there's nothing to step across.

---

```

| 9 | Decimal / float | `15000.5` | Reject |
| 10 | Empty / null | `` | Reject |

### Notes
- Cases 1–6 are the core BVA cases (min−1, min, min+1, max−1, max, max+1)
- Cases 7–10 cover type/format validation implied by "integer" constraint
- If your system allows leading zeros or formatted strings like `"15,000"`, add a case for that depending on your input type
---

## Input Analysis

- **Field**: Comments
- **Type**: Free text (string)

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is **not the appropriate technique** for a free-text field like "comments." BVA is designed for fields with **numeric or time ranges** where you can test values just below, at, and just above a boundary.

---

## What to Use Instead

Here are better techniques for a "comments" field:

| Technique | Best For |
|---|---|
| **Equivalence Partitioning** | Grouping valid/invalid input classes (e.g., empty, normal text, special characters) |
| **BVA on length** | If there's a **character limit** (e.g., max 500 characters) — this *is* numeric and BVA applies! |
| **Exploratory Testing** | Edge cases like emoji, HTML/script injection, Unicode, line breaks |
| **Decision Table Testing** | If comments behave differently based on other conditions |

---

## How I Can Help

**Option 1 — Does your comments field have a character limit?**
If yes (e.g., "max 500 characters" or "between 10 and 1000 characters"), tell me the range and I'll generate full BVA test cases on the **length** boundary.

**Option 2 — Want Equivalence Partitioning test cases instead?**
I can generate test cases covering input classes like empty input, normal text, max-length text, special characters, and more.

Which would you like to proceed with?

## BVA Test Cases: Age Validation (not over 65)

The boundary is at **65**. BVA tests the boundary itself and values immediately adjacent.

| Test Case | Input Age | Expected Result | Rationale |
|-----------|-----------|-----------------|-----------|
| TC-01 | 0 | Valid | Lower boundary (minimum valid age) |
| TC-02 | 1 | Valid | Just above lower boundary |
| TC-03 | 64 | Valid | Just below upper boundary |
| TC-04 | 65 | Valid | At upper boundary (inclusive) |
| TC-05 | 66 | Invalid | Just above upper boundary |
| TC-06 | -1 | Invalid | Below lower boundary |

### Partition summary

```
Invalid       | Valid          | Invalid
age < 0       | 0 <= age <= 65 | age > 65
              |                |
-1   [0]   1  ...  64  [65]  66
```

**Key BVA points:**
- `65` — boundary itself (valid, must be accepted)
- `66` — one step over (invalid, must be rejected)
- `64` — one step under boundary (valid)
- `0` / `-1` — lower boundary pair (valid/invalid)

> If the business also enforces a minimum age (e.g., 18), add boundary pairs at `17` (invalid) and `18` (valid).

You are improving an AI agent skill based on eval results and human feedback.

## Current SKILL.md
```markdown
---
name: test-engineer
description: >
  Helps business users and technical users analyze requirements with numeric or time inputs,
  then generates test cases and test data using Boundary Value Analysis (BVA) technique.
  Use when the user asks for test cases, test data, BVA, boundary testing, or wants to
  verify input fields with numeric ranges or time ranges.
license: Apache-2.0
metadata:
  author: bomb-skills
  version: "0.1"
---

## Overview

You are a test engineer assistant that uses **Boundary Value Analysis (BVA)** to generate test cases for input fields with numeric or time boundaries. Your goal is to save users time by automatically identifying boundaries and generating structured, ready-to-use test cases.

## When to Activate

Activate when the user:
- Asks for test cases for a field with a numeric or time range
- Mentions boundary value analysis, BVA, or boundary testing
- Provides requirements with min/max constraints on inputs
- Wants to verify input validation for numeric or time fields

## Instructions

### Step 1: Analyze the Requirement

Read the user's requirement and identify:
- **Input type**: numeric (integer or decimal) or time (HH:MM or HH:MM:SS)
- **Minimum value**: the lowest valid value
- **Maximum value**: the highest valid value
- **Precision**: integer, decimal places, or time unit (minutes/seconds)

If the input is not numeric or time-based (e.g., free text, dropdowns), inform the user that BVA is not the appropriate technique and suggest alternatives like Equivalence Partitioning or exploratory testing.

If the minimum value is greater than the maximum value, flag this as a likely error and ask the user to clarify before proceeding.

If there are multiple input fields, analyze each field separately and organize the output by field.

#### Ambiguous Precision / Minimum Unit

If the requirement does **not** make the minimum unit (precision/step size) clear, do NOT assume a default. Instead, ask the user to clarify before generating test cases. The minimum unit determines the "1 step" used in BVA and directly changes the test data.

**When precision IS clear** — go ahead and generate test cases without asking:
- The user specifies the format explicitly (e.g., "integer", "2 decimal places", "HH:MM")
- The user provides boundary values with a visible format (e.g., "09:00 to 17:00" implies HH:MM, "0.01 to 9999.99" implies 2 decimals)
- The context is unambiguous for domains without multiple interpretations (e.g., "quantity 1 to 100" is clearly integer — there's no alternative interpretation)

**When precision IS ambiguous** — always ask the user before proceeding:
- **Age** — always ambiguous, even if given as integers like "18 to 60". Age could mean: (a) user types age as a whole number, or (b) user enters a birthdate and the system calculates age in years-months-days. These produce very different boundary values. Always ask.
- **Money** — ambiguous unless decimal places are explicit. "Limit 30,000 baht" could mean step of 0.01, 1, or 100.
- **Percentage** — ambiguous unless format is stated. Could be integer (step=1) or decimal (step=0.01).
- Any domain where the data type could reasonably be interpreted multiple ways.

When asking:
1. Identify that the precision is ambiguous.
2. Show the user **concrete examples** of how different precision choices produce different boundary values.
3. Ask them to confirm which precision matches their system.
4. Wait for the user's response before generating test cases.

Common ambiguous cases:
- **Age**: Is the input a whole number of years (step = 1 year), or a birthdate where age is calculated in years-months-days? If birthdate, the boundary is not "64 years" but "64 years, 11 months, 29 days" — which means the actual input field is a date, not a number.
- **Money**: Is the minimum unit 0.01 (satang/cents), 1 (whole baht/dollars), or a larger denomination like 100? For a limit of 30,000: step=0.01 gives 29,999.99, step=1 gives 29,999, step=100 gives 29,900.
- **Percentage**: Is it integer (step=1) or decimal (step=0.01, 0.1)?

#### Single-Bound Requirements

If the requirement specifies **only a lower limit** (e.g., "must be at least 0") or **only an upper limit** (e.g., "cannot exceed 50"), do NOT generate the full BVA table immediately. Instead:

1. Tell the user which bound you found (lower or upper) and its value.
2. Ask the user to confirm or provide the missing bound. For example:
   - "I found a lower limit of 0, but no upper limit. What is the maximum allowed value for this field?"
   - "I found an upper limit of 50%, but no lower limit. What is the minimum allowed value? (e.g., 0?)"
3. Wait for the user's response before generating test cases.
4. Once both bounds are confirmed, proceed to Step 2 as normal.

### Step 2: Apply BVA Technique

For each identified boundary (min, max), generate these **6 core boundary values**:

| Position | Value | Expected Result |
|---|---|---|
| Just below minimum | min - 1 step | Invalid |
| Minimum (boundary) | min | Valid |
| Just above minimum | min + 1 step | Valid |
| Just below maximum | max - 1 step | Valid |
| Maximum (boundary) | max | Valid |
| Just above maximum | max + 1 step | Invalid |

Where "1 step" depends on precision:
- **Integer**: step = 1
- **Decimal (N places)**: step = 10^(-N) (e.g., 2 decimal places → 0.01)
- **Time (HH:MM)**: step = 1 minute
- **Time (HH:MM:SS)**: step = 1 second

### Step 3: Generate Output

Present the test cases in a **markdown table** with these 5 columns:

| ID | Name | Description | Input | Expected Output |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| TC-01 | {short name} | {business description} | {value} | {result} |

Column definitions:
- **ID**: Sequential test case ID (TC-01, TC-02, ...)
- **Name**: Short name describing what this test case covers (e.g., "Below minimum age", "Maximum boundary")
- **Description**: Business-understandable explanation of what is being tested and what should happen. Write it so a non-technical person can understand the purpose. Example: "Enter age 17, which is one below the minimum allowed age of 18. The system should reject this input."
- **Input**: The concrete test data value, ready to copy-paste
- **Expected Output**: Whether the system should accept or reject the value (e.g., "Invalid - rejected", "Valid - accepted")

## Example

**User prompt**: "Age field accepts 18 to 60"

**Output**:

**Input Analysis**
- Field: Age
- Type: Numeric (integer)
- Range: 18 to 60

**BVA Test Cases**

| ID | Name | Description | Input | Expected Output |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| TC-01 | Below minimum age | Enter age 17, which is one below the minimum allowed age of 18. The system should reject this input. | 17 | Invalid - rejected |
| TC-02 | Minimum age boundary | Enter age 18, which is the lowest allowed age. The system should accept this input. | 18 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-03 | Above minimum age | Enter age 19, which is just above the minimum. The system should accept this input. | 19 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-04 | Below maximum age | Enter age 59, which is just below the maximum allowed age of 60. The system should accept this input. | 59 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-05 | Maximum age boundary | Enter age 60, which is the highest allowed age. The system should accept this input. | 60 | Valid - accepted |
| TC-06 | Above maximum age | Enter age 61, which is one above the maximum allowed age of 60. The system should reject this input. | 61 | Invalid - rejected |

## Example: Single-Bound Requirement

**User prompt**: "The score field must be at least 0. Generate BVA test cases."

**Output**:

**Input Analysis**
- Field: Score
- Type: Numeric
- Lower limit: 0
- Upper limit: **not specified**

I found a lower limit of **0**, but no upper limit was provided. To generate complete BVA test cases, I need both boundaries.

**Could you confirm the maximum allowed value for the score field?** For example, is it 100, 999, or something else?

## Example: Ambiguous Precision

**User prompt**: "Registration requires users to be not over 65 years old. Create BVA test cases."

**Output**:

**Input Analysis**
- Field: Age
- Constraint: not over 65 years old
- Precision: **unclear — need to clarify**

Before I generate test cases, I need to clarify the **minimum unit of age data** in your system, because it changes the boundary values significantly:

| If the input is... | Step size | Boundary just below 65 | Boundary at 65 | Boundary just above 65 |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Age as whole years (integer) | 1 year | 64 | 65 | 66 |
| Birthdate (year-month-day) | 1 day | 64 years, 11 months, 29 days | Exactly 65 years | 65 years, 0 months, 1 day |

**How does your system capture age?**
- Does the user enter their age as a number (e.g., "64")? → I'll use integer step of 1 year.
- Does the user enter a birthdate and the system calculates age? → I'll use date-based boundaries and the input field is actually a date.

## Example: Ambiguous Money Precision

**User prompt**: "Daily deposit limit is not over 30,000 baht. Generate BVA test cases."

**Output**:

**Input Analysis**
- Field: Deposit amount
- Constraint: not over 30,000 baht
- Precision: **unclear — need to clarify**

Before I generate test cases, I need to clarify the **minimum unit of money** your system accepts:

| If the minimum unit is... | Boundary just below 30,000 | At 30,000 | Just above 30,000 |
|---|---|---|---|
| 0.01 (satang) | 29,999.99 | 30,000.00 | 30,000.01 |
| 1 (whole baht) | 29,999 | 30,000 | 30,001 |
| 100 (hundred baht) | 29,900 | 30,000 | 30,100 |

**What is the smallest amount a user can deposit?** For example, can they deposit 0.01 baht (satang), or only whole baht, or only multiples of 100?

```

| `0` | Reject | Zero |
| `-1` | Reject | Negative number |

| Input | Expected | Technique |
|-------|----------|-----------|
| `18.5` | Reject | Decimal (field requires integer) |
| `"twenty"` | Reject | String |
| `""` | Reject | Empty input |
| `" "` | Reject | Whitespace only |
| `null` | Reject | No value submitted |
| `18abc` | Reject | Alphanumeric |
| `1e2` | Reject | Scientific notation (evaluates to 100) |

| Input | Expected | Technique |
|-------|----------|-----------|
| `018` | Accept or Reject | Leading zero — depends on whether you parse as octal or strip it |
| `+18` | Accept or Reject | Leading plus sign |
| `2147483647` | Reject | Integer overflow (MAX_INT) |

## USER (2026-03-28 02:45:07)

Grade each assertion against the actual output below.
For each assertion, respond with PASS or FAIL and brief evidence.

ACTUAL OUTPUT:
---
**Input Analysis**
- Field: Comments
- Type: Free text

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is designed for **numeric or time-based inputs** where there are minimum and maximum numeric boundaries. A "comments" field is free text, so BVA does not apply here.

**Why BVA doesn't fit:**
BVA works by testing values just below, at, and just above a numeric boundary (e.g., min/max age, price range, time window). Free text fields don't have a natural numeric boundary to probe in the same way.

---

**Better techniques for a comments field:**

| Technique | What it tests |
|---|---|
| **Equivalence Partitioning** | Group inputs into valid/invalid classes (e.g., non-empty vs. empty, allowed characters vs. special characters) |
| **Length boundary testing** | If there is a character limit (e.g., max 500 chars), BVA *can* apply — but only to the **length** of the text, not the content |
| **Exploratory / negative testing** | SQL injection, HTML tags, emojis, very long strings, whitespace-only input |

---

**To proceed, I have two questions:**

1. Does your comments field have a **character limit** (e.g., max 255 or 500 characters)? If yes, I can apply BVA to the **length** boundary and generate test cases for that.

2. Is the field **required or optional**? This helps determine whether an empty input is a valid or invalid test case.

Please share the constraints and I'll generate the appropriate test cases right away.
---

ASSERTIONS:
1. The output recognizes that a free-text field is not suitable for BVA
2. The output asks for clarification or suggests alternative testing techniques

Respond in this exact JSON format (no markdown, no code fences):
{
  "assertion_results": [
    {"text": "assertion text", "passed": true/false, "evidence": "brief quote or reason"}
  ]
}

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is not the appropriate technique for a free-text field like "comments" because BVA applies to **numeric or time-based inputs** where there are clear minimum and maximum values with a measurable step size.

**However**, if your "comments" field has a **character length limit** (e.g., "must be between 1 and 500 characters"), then BVA *can* be applied — treating the character count as the numeric boundary.

---

**What would you like to do?**

**Option 1 — Apply BVA to character length**
Tell me the character limit for the comments field. For example:
- "Minimum 1 character, maximum 500 characters"
- "Cannot exceed 255 characters"

I'll then generate BVA test cases based on the length boundaries.

**Option 2 — Use a different testing technique**
For free-text content (not length), other techniques are more appropriate:

| Technique | Best for |
|---|---|
| **Equivalence Partitioning** | Valid vs. invalid content categories (e.g., empty, normal text, special characters) |
| **Exploratory Testing** | Edge cases like emoji, HTML/script injection, multi-line input, copy-paste |
| **Decision Table Testing** | When field behavior depends on combinations of conditions |

Could you clarify whether the comments field has a **character length constraint**, or describe what validation rules apply? That will help me generate the most useful test cases for you.

## USER (2026-03-28 02:56:06)

Grade each assertion against the actual output below.
For each assertion, respond with PASS or FAIL and brief evidence.

ACTUAL OUTPUT:
---
**Input Analysis**
- Field: Comments
- Type: Free text

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is not the appropriate technique for a free-text field like "comments." BVA works specifically with **numeric ranges** or **time ranges** — where you can define a minimum and maximum value and step through boundaries.

For a comments field, the input space is not ordered or bounded in the same way, so there are no meaningful "boundary values" to test.

---

**Better techniques for a comments field:**

Here are techniques that are actually well-suited for this type of field:

1. **Equivalence Partitioning** — Divide inputs into valid/invalid classes, e.g.:
   - Valid: normal text, text with special characters, multilingual text
   - Invalid: input that exceeds max length (if there's a character limit)

2. **Length/character limit testing** — If the field has a max character count (e.g., 500 characters), then BVA *does* apply to the **length** of the input. For example, testing at 499, 500, and 501 characters.

3. **Exploratory / special character testing** — Test inputs like empty string, whitespace only, SQL injection strings, HTML/script tags, emoji, very long text, Unicode characters.

---

**Does your comments field have a character limit?**

If yes, I can apply BVA to the **length** of the input and generate proper boundary test cases for you.

1. Yes — it has a maximum character limit (please tell me the limit)
2. Yes — it has both a minimum and maximum character limit (please tell me both)
3. No — there is no character limit
4. Other — please specify: ___
---

ASSERTIONS:
1. The output recognizes that a free-text field is not suitable for BVA
2. The output asks for clarification or suggests alternative testing techniques

Respond in this exact JSON format (no markdown, no code fences):
{
  "assertion_results": [
    {"text": "assertion text", "passed": true/false, "evidence": "brief quote or reason"}
  ]
}

Grade each assertion against the actual output below.

ACTUAL OUTPUT:
---
**Input Analysis**
- Field: Comments
- Type: Free text

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is designed for **numeric or time-based inputs** where you can define a minimum and maximum value with a measurable step between them.

A "comments" field is free text, so there are no numeric boundaries to test in the traditional BVA sense. Applying BVA here would not be meaningful or useful.

**Recommended techniques for a free-text field instead:**

- **Equivalence Partitioning** — group inputs into valid/invalid classes (e.g., non-empty text, empty/blank, special characters, very long strings)
- **Boundary Value Analysis on length** — if the field has a character limit (e.g., max 500 characters), BVA *can* apply to the **length constraint**, not the content itself
- **Exploratory Testing** — manually probe edge cases like SQL injection, HTML tags, emoji, line breaks, null characters, etc.

---

**Does your "comments" field have a character length limit?**

If yes, I can apply BVA to the **length** of the input (e.g., min/max characters allowed). Just tell me the limit — for example:

- "Comments must be between 10 and 500 characters"
- "Comments cannot exceed 255 characters"

Share the length constraints and I'll generate BVA test cases right away.

| Input | Expected | Technique |
|-------|----------|-----------|

| `1e2` | Rejected | Scientific notation |
| Very long string (e.g. 1000 chars) | Rejected | Buffer/overflow check |

ACTUAL OUTPUT:
---
**Input Analysis**
- Field: Comments
- Type: Free text

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is designed for **numeric or time-based inputs** where you can define a minimum and maximum value with a measurable step size. A "comments" field is free text, so there are no numeric boundaries to test — BVA does not apply here.

**Better techniques for a free-text comments field:**

- **Equivalence Partitioning** — Group inputs into classes like: empty input, normal text, very long text, special characters, unicode/emoji, whitespace-only. Test one representative from each class.
- **Boundary Value Analysis (length limit)** — BVA *can* apply if your comments field has a **character limit** (e.g., max 500 characters). In that case, the boundary is the character count, not the content. If you have a length limit, share it and I can generate BVA test cases based on that.
- **Exploratory Testing** — Manually probe edge cases like SQL injection, HTML/script tags, null bytes, or copy-pasted content with hidden characters.

---

Do you have a **character length limit** on the comments field? If so, tell me the limit (e.g., "max 500 characters") and I can apply BVA to the length boundary right away.
---

2. The output asks for clarification or suggests alternative testing techniques

**Boundaries identified:**

- **Lower boundary:** 0/1 — age cannot be zero or negative
- **Upper boundary:** 65/66 — the critical rule boundary

**Key BVA principle applied:** Test the value at the boundary (65), one below (64), and one above (66) — these are the most likely points for off-by-one defects (e.g., a buggy check using `> 65` vs `>= 65` vs `> 64`).

Here are test cases for a booking system time input (09:00–17:00):

## Boundary Value Analysis

| Test ID | Input | Expected | Category |
|---------|-------|----------|----------|
| T01 | `09:00` | Accept | Lower boundary |
| T02 | `17:00` | Accept | Upper boundary |
| T03 | `08:59` | Reject | Just below lower boundary |
| T04 | `17:01` | Reject | Just above upper boundary |
| T05 | `13:00` | Accept | Mid-range (nominal) |

## Equivalence Partitions

| Test ID | Input | Expected | Category |
|---------|-------|----------|----------|
| T06 | `10:30` | Accept | Valid — inside range |
| T07 | `07:00` | Reject | Invalid — before open |
| T08 | `19:00` | Reject | Invalid — after close |
| T09 | `00:00` | Reject | Midnight |
| T10 | `23:59` | Reject | End of day |

## Format & Edge Cases

| Test ID | Input | Expected | Category |
|---------|-------|----------|----------|
| T11 | `9:00` | Reject or normalize | Missing leading zero |
| T12 | `09:60` | Reject | Invalid minutes |
| T13 | `09:00 AM` | Reject | 12-hour format |
| T14 | `9am` | Reject | Informal format |
| T15 | `09-00` | Reject | Wrong separator |
| T16 | `0900` | Reject | Missing separator |
| T17 | `` (empty) | Reject | Empty input |
| T18 | `abc` | Reject | Non-numeric |
| T19 | `09:00:00` | Reject or accept | Seconds included |
| T20 | `  09:00  ` | Accept or reject | Leading/trailing whitespace |

- Are bookings on the hour only, or any minute (e.g., `09:15`, `09:07`)?
- Is `17:00` a valid *start* time (i.e., can someone book a 1-hour slot ending at 18:00)?
- Should the system normalize near-valid formats (T11, T20) or strictly reject them?

The answers will determine whether T11 and T20 are accept or reject, and may add cases like `09:07` vs `09:15` depending on slot granularity.

---
**Input Analysis**
- Field: Comments
- Type: Free text

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is designed for fields with **numeric or time-based ranges** — it works by testing values just below, at, and just above a minimum or maximum boundary.

A **comments field** is free text, so there are no numeric or time boundaries to analyze with BVA. Applying BVA here would not be meaningful.

---

**Recommended alternatives for a text field:**

| Technique | Best for |
|---|---|
| **Equivalence Partitioning** | Grouping valid/invalid inputs (e.g., empty, normal text, special characters) |
| **Boundary Value Analysis (length)** | If the field has a **character limit** (e.g., max 500 chars) — BVA *can* apply to the length constraint |
| **Exploratory Testing** | Uncovering unexpected behavior with edge-case text inputs |

---

**Does your comments field have a character length limit?**

- 0 characters (empty)

- 501 characters (over limit)

| Input | Expected | Reason |
|-------|----------|--------|

| Input | Expected | Reason |
|-------|----------|--------|
| `9:00` | Reject/Normalize | Missing leading zero |
| `09:0` | Reject | Malformed minutes |
| `0900` | Reject | No colon separator |
| `9am` | Reject | 12-hour format |
| `09:60` | Reject | Invalid minutes (≥60) |
| `24:00` | Reject | Invalid hour |
| `25:00` | Reject | Hour out of range |
| `-01:00` | Reject | Negative time |
| `abc` | Reject | Non-numeric |
| `` (empty) | Reject | Missing input |
| `null` / `undefined` | Reject | No value |

| Input | Expected | Reason |
|-------|----------|--------|
| `00:00` | Reject | Midnight — outside range |
| `17:00:00` | Reject/Normalize | Seconds included |
| `09:00 ` | Accept/Normalize | Trailing whitespace |
| ` 09:00` | Accept/Normalize | Leading whitespace |
| `09:00 AM` | Reject/Normalize | 12-hour with AM/PM |

- **17:00 is accepted** — confirm whether end-of-day means "start of 17:00 slot" or "no bookings at 17:00" (a common ambiguity)

## USER (2026-03-28 03:29:50)

Grade each assertion against the actual output below.
For each assertion, respond with PASS or FAIL and brief evidence.

ACTUAL OUTPUT:
---
**Input Analysis**
- Field: Comments
- Type: Free text (string)

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is designed for **numeric or time-based inputs** where you can define a minimum and maximum value with a measurable step size. A free-text "comments" field does not have numeric or time boundaries, so BVA is not the right technique here.

**Suggested alternatives for a comments field:**

- **Equivalence Partitioning (EP)** — Divide inputs into valid/invalid classes, e.g.:
  - Valid: any non-empty text within the allowed length
  - Invalid: empty input (if required), input exceeding max length, special characters (if restricted), script injection attempts (XSS)

- **Length-based BVA** — If your comments field has a **character limit** (e.g., max 500 characters), then BVA *does* apply to the **length** of the input. In that case, let me know the min/max character count and I can generate test cases like:
  - 0 characters (empty)
  - 1 character
  - 499 characters
  - 500 characters (boundary)
  - 501 characters (over limit)

- **Exploratory Testing** — Useful for catching unexpected behavior with edge-case content (emoji, line breaks, HTML tags, SQL injection strings, etc.)

---

Does your comments field have a **character length limit**? If so, share the min/max length and I'll generate BVA test cases based on that. Otherwise, I can help you design Equivalence Partitioning test cases instead.
---

ASSERTIONS:
1. The output recognizes that a free-text field is not suitable for BVA
2. The output asks for clarification or suggests alternative testing techniques

Respond in this exact JSON format (no markdown, no code fences):
{
  "assertion_results": [
    {"text": "assertion text", "passed": true/false, "evidence": "brief quote or reason"}
  ]
}

|-------|------|----------|
| `018` | Leading zero | Reject or normalize to `18` (define behavior) |
| `+18` | Leading plus sign | Reject or normalize to `18` (define behavior) |
| Very large number (e.g., `99999999`) | Integer overflow | Reject |

Here are test cases covering the key boundaries and edge cases:

## Valid Times (should accept)

| `09:01` | Just above lower boundary |
| `12:00` | Midpoint |

## Invalid Times (should reject)
| Input | Description |
|-------|-------------|

| `17:01` | Just above upper boundary |

## Invalid Format (should reject)
| Input | Description |
|-------|-------------|

| `09:0` | Incomplete minutes |

| `09:60` | Minutes out of range |
| `25:00` | Hours out of range |
| `09:00:00` | Extra seconds component |
| `9am` | Non-24h format |
| `abc` | Non-numeric |
| `` | Empty string |
| `null` / `undefined` | Null input |

## Edge Cases
| Input | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| ` 09:00` | Leading whitespace |
| `09:00 ` | Trailing whitespace |
| `09:00 AM` | 12h format with AM/PM |

---

The most critical cases are the **boundary values** (`08:59`, `09:00`, `17:00`, `17:01`) — these catch off-by-one errors in range checks. Want me to scaffold these as actual test code in a specific framework?

Here are test cases covering boundary values, equivalence partitions, and edge cases:

## Valid Cases (should accept)

| Input | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `18` | Boundary | Minimum valid age |
| `19` | Near boundary | Just above minimum |
| `30` | Valid partition | Mid-range value |
| `59` | Near boundary | Just below maximum |
| `60` | Boundary | Maximum valid age |

## Invalid — Out of Range (should reject)

| Input | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `17` | Boundary | One below minimum |
| `61` | Boundary | One above maximum |
| `0` | Edge | Zero |
| `-1` | Edge | Negative number |
| `150` | Edge | Unrealistically large |

## Invalid — Wrong Type (should reject)

| Input | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `18.5` | Edge | Decimal/float |
| `"eighteen"` | Edge | String text |
| `""` | Edge | Empty input |
| `" "` | Edge | Whitespace only |
| `null` / not provided | Edge | Missing value |
| `18abc` | Edge | Alphanumeric |

## Key principles applied

- **Boundary Value Analysis** — test at `18`, `17`, `60`, `61` (the edges and their neighbors)
- **Equivalence Partitioning** — one valid mid-range value is sufficient to represent the whole valid partition
- **Invalid type inputs** — important if the field accepts free text entry before validation

ACTUAL OUTPUT:
---
**Input Analysis**
- Field: Comments
- Type: Free text

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is designed for fields with **numeric or time-based ranges** — it works by testing values just below, at, and just above a boundary (e.g., min/max age, price limits, time windows).

A free-text "comments" field doesn't have a numeric boundary to test against, so BVA is not the right technique here.

**Better alternatives for a comments field:**

| Technique | What it tests | Example test cases |
|---|---|---|
| **Equivalence Partitioning** | Groups of valid/invalid inputs | Empty, normal text, very long text, special characters |
| **Length boundary testing** | If there's a character limit (e.g., max 500 chars) | BVA *can* apply here — test at 499, 500, 501 chars |
| **Exploratory Testing** | Edge-case content behavior | Emojis, HTML tags, SQL injection strings, newlines |

**I can help you with BVA if your comments field has a character limit.** For example, if comments must be between 10 and 500 characters, I can generate a full BVA test case table for that.

Does your comments field have a **minimum or maximum character length** constraint? If so, share it and I'll generate the test cases right away.
---

ASSERTIONS:
1. The output recognizes that a free-text field is not suitable for BVA
2. The output asks for clarification or suggests alternative testing techniques

Respond in this exact JSON format (no markdown, no code fences):
{
  "assertion_results": [
    {"text": "assertion text", "passed": true/false, "evidence": "brief quote or reason"}
  ]
}

| TC ID | Input (Age) | Expected Result | Rationale |
|-------|-------------|-----------------|-----------|
| TC-01 | -1 | Reject | Below minimum possible age (invalid input) |
| TC-02 | 0 | Reject | Boundary just above invalid — likely minimum valid age edge |
| TC-03 | 1 | Accept | Minimum plausible valid age |
| TC-04 | 64 | Accept | One below upper boundary |
| TC-05 | 65 | Accept | **Upper boundary** — must be accepted ("not over 65") |
| TC-06 | 66 | Reject | **One above upper boundary** — must be rejected |
| TC-07 | 67 | Reject | Two above upper boundary (general invalid zone) |

### Key Boundary Points

```
Invalid  |  Valid      |  Invalid
---------|-------------|----------
...  0   |  1  ...  65 |  66  ...
```

- **TC-05 (age=65)** and **TC-06 (age=66)** are the critical BVA pair — they straddle the exact cutoff.
- TC-04 and TC-06 confirm the boundary behaves correctly on both sides.
- TC-01/TC-02 cover invalid negative/zero inputs that should also be rejected regardless of the age rule.

## USER (2026-03-28 04:02:32)

Grade each assertion against the actual output below.
For each assertion, respond with PASS or FAIL and brief evidence.

ACTUAL OUTPUT:
---
**Input Analysis**
- Field: Comments
- Type: Free text

BVA (Boundary Value Analysis) is designed for **numeric or time-based inputs** where you can define a minimum and maximum value with a measurable step size. A free-text "comments" field doesn't have numeric boundaries, so BVA is not the right technique here.

**Better alternatives for a comments field:**

- **Equivalence Partitioning** — Group inputs into valid/invalid classes, e.g.:
  - Valid: non-empty text within allowed length
  - Invalid: empty/blank, exceeds max length, contains forbidden characters

- **Boundary Value Analysis on length** — If your comments field has a **character limit** (e.g., max 500 characters), then BVA *does* apply to the length constraint. For example, if the field accepts 1–500 characters, I can generate test cases for lengths 0, 1, 2, 499, 500, and 501.

- **Exploratory Testing** — Test special characters, HTML/script injection, Unicode, emojis, line breaks, etc.

---

**Does your comments field have a minimum or maximum character length?** If so, share the constraint and I'll generate BVA test cases on the length boundary right away.
---

ASSERTIONS:
1. The output recognizes that a free-text field is not suitable for BVA
2. The output asks for clarification or suggests alternative testing techniques

Respond in this exact JSON format (no markdown, no code fences):
{
  "assertion_results": [
    {"text": "assertion text", "passed": true/false, "evidence": "brief quote or reason"}
  ]
}

| TC-14 | Leading/trailing spaces | `"  comment  "` | Check if trimmed before validation |
